  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7e4b5178-7517-4c9d-9d09-7e3d9603d941'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

Nope.<br/><br/>It was the most boring novella I've read for a YA fantasy book. <b>Farley's</b> character is dull and boring. The only one that made this novella quite interesting is <b>Shade Barrow</b>, but everything is disappointing.<br/><br/>I don't know if I'm the only one who has this problem, but the narrative reports by the <i>Scarlet Guard</i> are too difficult to comprehend. I don't even know what those are all about. They are too technical!<br/><br/>I expected some reve</span>
  <span id="freeText14717012548499007838" style="display:none">I thought by reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25362018.Steel_Scars__Red_Queen___0_2_" title="Steel Scars (Red Queen, #0.2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Steel Scars</a> I would be in for a badass story. Nope.<br><br>It was the most boring novella I've read for a YA fantasy book. <b>Farley's</b> character is dull and boring. The only one that made this novella quite interesting is <b>Shade Barrow</b>, but everything is disappointing.<br><br>I don't know if I'm the only one who has this problem, but the narrative reports by the <i>Scarlet Guard</i> are too difficult to comprehend. I don't even know what those are all about. They are too technical!<br><br>I expected some revelations and actions scenes. <span id="freeTextContainer2721630052417586915"><u>2 Red as the dawn ★'s</u> <br/><br/><i>“Will you oath yourself to the Scarlet Guard?” <br/>“On one condition.” <br/>“The Guard does not bargain.” <br/>“This isn't a request to the Guard, but to you.” <br/>“And that is?” <br/>"What's your name?” <br/>“My name is Diana... <br/>Are you with us, Shade Barrow?"<br/>“I'm with you, Diana.” <br/><b>“Then we will rise.” <br/>“Red as the dawn.”</b> </i><br/><br/>Novellas have never been my thing but I was really hoping this would be as good as <i>Queen Song (o.1)</i> but it wasn't. Anyways, that being said this novella is Farleys POV. Farley has ne</span>
  <span id="freeText2721630052417586915" style="display:none"><u>2 Red as the dawn ★'s</u> <br /><br /><i>“Will you oath yourself to the Scarlet Guard?” <br />“On one condition.” <br />“The Guard does not bargain.” <br />“This isn't a request to the Guard, but to you.” <br />“And that is?” <br />"What's your name?” <br />“My name is Diana... <br />Are you with us, Shade Barrow?"<br />“I'm with you, Diana.” <br /><b>“Then we will rise.” <br />“Red as the dawn.”</b> </i><br /><br />Novellas have never been my thing but I was really hoping this would be as good as <i>Queen Song (o.1)</i> but it wasn't. Anyways, that being said this novella is Farleys POV. Farley has never been a favorite character of mine but it was kinda cool being able to see some earlier operations that lead up to <i>Red Queen</i>. I loved getting to seeing how Farley and Shade met. I've always loved Shade and I wish Victoria Aveyard would have pushed that further. For the most part, I found it to be repetitive and boring. Wish this was Shades POV instead.</span>

    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1726907002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13729985500260126319">Steel Scars (Red Queen 0.2), Victoria Aveyard<br/>In this digital prequel novella set in the Red Queen world, Captain Farley exchanges coded transmissions with the resistance as she travels the land recruiting black market traders, smugglers, and extremists for her first attempt at an attack on the capital. She was raised to be strong, but planting the seeds of rebellion in Norta is a tougher job than expected—until she stumbles upon a connection that may prove to be the key to the entire operation: </span>
  <span id="freeText13729985500260126319" style="display:none">Steel Scars (Red Queen 0.2), Victoria Aveyard<br />In this digital prequel novella set in the Red Queen world, Captain Farley exchanges coded transmissions with the resistance as she travels the land recruiting black market traders, smugglers, and extremists for her first attempt at an attack on the capital. She was raised to be strong, but planting the seeds of rebellion in Norta is a tougher job than expected—until she stumbles upon a connection that may prove to be the key to the entire operation: Mare Barrow.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: دهم ماه سپتامبر سال 2016 میلادی<br />عنوان: زخمهای پولادین - کتاب 0.2 - مجموعه ملکه سرخ؛ نویسنده: ویکتوریا آویارد؛ مترجم: محمدصالح نورانی زاده؛ تهران، کتابسرای تندیس؛ 1394؛ در 126 ص؛ مصور؛ شابک: 9786001821950؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی قرن 21 م<br />مجموعه‌ «ملکه سرخ» یک مجموعه‌ فانتزی شش جلدی است که چهار جلد آن، به عنوان سری اصلی، و دو جلد دیگر آن به عنوان سری فرعی شناخته می‌شوند. خلاصه داستان این رمان: «سروان فارلی همچنانکه با نیروهای مقاومت تبادل اطلاعات می‌کند، برلی برای آغاز نخستین اقدام شورشی‌ خویش در پایتخت سفر می‌کند و به دنبال استخدام تاجران بازار سیاه، قاچاقچیان و افراط گرایانی می‌گردد که بتوانند یاریش کنند. او یاد گرفته همیشه مستقل و قوی باشد، اما کاشتن دانه‌ های انقلاب در «نورتا» به آن آسانی که به نظر می‌رسید نیست؛ البته تا زمانی...». ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="13729985500260126319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047872701" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047872701?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047872701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17766843954127092027">Okay, folks, let’s keep this short and simple!<br/><br/>I’m usually a huge fan of Victoria Aveyard’s books but “Steel Scars” definitely wasn’t my cup of tea. Since it was from Farley’s POV I expected to find out more about how she and Shade met and how they fell in love. Much to my chagrin this unfortunately didn’t happen though and probably is the reason why I was so disappointed in the end. =((((<br/><br/><b>What I expected:</b><br/>-	The background story about how Farley and Shade met<br/>-	Details about them falling in love <br/>-	I</span>
  <span id="freeText17766843954127092027" style="display:none">Okay, folks, let’s keep this short and simple!<br /><br />I’m usually a huge fan of Victoria Aveyard’s books but “Steel Scars” definitely wasn’t my cup of tea. Since it was from Farley’s POV I expected to find out more about how she and Shade met and how they fell in love. Much to my chagrin this unfortunately didn’t happen though and probably is the reason why I was so disappointed in the end. =((((<br /><br /><b>What I expected:</b><br />-	The background story about how Farley and Shade met<br />-	Details about them falling in love <br />-	Information about what exactly happened to Farley’s mother and her sister<br />-	More insight about her tense relationship with the Colonel <br />-	More Shade!!!! <br /><br /><b>What I got:</b><br />-	The background story about how Farley and Shade met<br />-	Almost <u>no details</u> about them falling in love<br />-	<u>No information</u> about what happened to Farley’s family<br />-	Only her tense relationship with the Colonel but <u>no insight why</u> it actually is that way…<br />-	<u>Too little of Shade!!!</u> His first appearance is in the middle of the novella and after that the Shade scenes still were pretty rare…<br /><br />I also didn’t like the military messages that always popped up and apparently were supposed to act as the beginning of chapters. <br />The only interesting parts were those in which Shade made an appearance and the fact that Farley’s codename was LAMB and the Colonel’s RAM. ;-)<br /><br />Overall the entire military feel made the book kind of boring to read and I’m sorry to say it, but I can’t recommend reading it. Better stick to the “Red Queen” series and “Queen Song”!<br /><br />Sorry Victoria!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17766843954127092027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donita Luz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donita Luz" href="/user/show/18877120-donita-luz">Donita Luz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1555999612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5813438607620364139"><blockquote>
  <i>"We succeed where others can't. We survive. Now I must do the same alone. Now I have to protect others, taking their lives-and deaths-onto my shoulders."</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Steel Cars</b>, on the other hand was so boooring I find myself dozing of a lot of times. It actually took me 3 days to finish reading it, a real feat, considering it was just a novella with more or less a 100 pages.<br/><br/>This Novella was from Farley's, The Scarlet Guard Captain's POV. I was really surprised since her character here was so different f</span>
  <span id="freeText5813438607620364139" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"We succeed where others can't. We survive. Now I must do the same alone. Now I have to protect others, taking their lives-and deaths-onto my shoulders."</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Steel Cars</b>, on the other hand was so boooring I find myself dozing of a lot of times. It actually took me 3 days to finish reading it, a real feat, considering it was just a novella with more or less a 100 pages.<br /><br />This Novella was from Farley's, The Scarlet Guard Captain's POV. I was really surprised since her character here was so different from the Farley I imagined on The Red Queen. She was only 22 years old and hungry to prove her worth to her commander, I totally thought she was a older than than. She was vulnerable totally different from the Farley from the first book that let the failed rebellion against the Silver and reading her POV was all sorts of boring. There weren't any real action you would expect from the leader of a rebellion! This short novella also left me confused as hell.<br /><br />I find it funny how Farley and all of her people can infiltrate and walk around the Stilts easily like they are from Norta. I mean, I remember Mare noting Farley as a Foreigner, a Lakelander, at first sight, so how can they walk around the Norta lands without raising any suspicion at all? I thought they were in war with the Lakelanders for the lands- the point of conscription in the first place right? That was the first war before the Scarlet Guard rage their own war against the Silver? For equality?<br /><br />Then there's all those decoded message from the Scarlet Guard. I won't even pretend to understand them because I didn't and I still don't. I didn't even bother remembering all their code names when they are using their real names all the time. <br /><br />Obviously, I have way too many issue with this novella to enjoy it. The only reason why it's gotten a 2 star rating from me was because of <b>Shade Barrow</b>. Yes, Mare Barrow charismatic brother and because of Farley and Shade's hinted romance in there that I've never really notice after reading 11 chapters from the Glass Sword <b>(Yes, I've read 8 chapters from the Glass Sword before I decided to read this novella firs. Don't judge me. lol)</b>. Remind me again why this novella wasn't about Shade or Maven instead? Oh yeah well, maybe for Girl Power? :|</span>
  <a data-text-id="5813438607620364139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <blockquote>6 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br/><a href='http://www.livelib.ru/review/586121' rel='nofollow noopener'>ревью на русском/review in russian</a><br/><br/>100 pages, nice length for a bonus! <br/><br/>Farley (this is a surname, btw) will tell you how she and her father came to Norta from Lakelands, what it's like to be a part of Scarlet Guard and how she started to recruit local Reds.   <span id="freeText15743060524033112092" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>6 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br /><a href="http://www.livelib.ru/review/586121" rel="nofollow noopener">ревью на русском/review in russian</a><br /><br />100 pages, nice length for a bonus! <br /><br />Farley (this is a surname, btw) will tell you how she and her father came to Norta from Lakelands, what it's like to be a part of Scarlet Guard and how she started to recruit local Reds. We won't know what exactly did Colonel Farley, how his wife and other daughter died, how he and Farley got their scars... I thought we would. <br /><br />For me the second 50 pages out of 100 were better and more interesting, 'cause there were Shade, Mare, Stilts, smth familiar and already cherished. <br /><br />For those who already read <i>Glass Sword</i> this story would have a bittersweet aftertaste. I actually cried at some parts. And you know what? I suggest you to read the series in this order: <i>Red Queen, Queen Song, Glass Sword</i> and only then <i>Steel Scars</i>. Some moments would be more surprising if you will find them out in <i>GS</i> while some would have more depth if you will read them after <i>GS</i>.<br /><br />All in all, I already liked Farley (after GS), so this bonus hasn't changed anything vital in our relationships. But again, for me and my feelings these 100 pages had such a treasure... not obvious, but really valuable one. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"My name is Diana."<br />For once, his smile is rea. No jokes, no mask.<br />"Are you with us, Shade Barrow?"<br />"I'm with you, Diana."<br />"Then we will rise."<br />His voice joins mine.<br />"Red as the dawn."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />And <i>this</i> was the name)<br /><br /><b>Red Queen (Алая королева):</b><br /><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219807950" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen Song (Песнь королевы)</a> #0.1/4<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1312174580" rel="nofollow noopener">Steel Scars (Стальные шрамы)</a> #0.2/4<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113268481" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469225994" rel="nofollow noopener">Алая Королева</a>) #1/4<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113268493" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Sword (Стеклянный меч</a>) #2/4<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113268496" rel="nofollow noopener">King's Cage (Королевская клетка)</a> #3/4<br />— Untitled (Без названия) #4/4</blockquote></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1309739670?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie">Carrie</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1309739670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9802385779050437560">Steel Scars is a companion novella to the Red Queen series by Victoria Aveyard. In this second of two novellas to be read between Red Queen and Glass Sword we get a closer look at Farley and the beginnings of the rebellion. Travelling the land recruiting for the rebellion it is shown here her stumbling upon meeting Mare Barrow. <br/><br/>Red Queen is already a series that I found could drag quite a bit when I was reading it but this novella was even worse. Farley just wasn't very interesting at all and th</span>
  <span id="freeText9802385779050437560" style="display:none">Steel Scars is a companion novella to the Red Queen series by Victoria Aveyard. In this second of two novellas to be read between Red Queen and Glass Sword we get a closer look at Farley and the beginnings of the rebellion. Travelling the land recruiting for the rebellion it is shown here her stumbling upon meeting Mare Barrow. <br /><br />Red Queen is already a series that I found could drag quite a bit when I was reading it but this novella was even worse. Farley just wasn't very interesting at all and the constant reports were rather dull to have over and over again, such a short read to begin with could have done without so many of those. Still nice to get a peek back into the series before picking up Glass Sword.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9802385779050437560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2397587296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer972261240917893766">Read in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25944381.Cruel_Crown__Red_Queen___0_1_0_2_' title='Cruel Crown (Red Queen, #0.1-0.2) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cruel Crown</a> bind up.<br/><br/>The second story is told from the point of view of Captain Farley and starts just before <b>Red Queen</b> with some overlap in the timeline which the main reason I think you should read the full length book first. I was really excited about this story and getting more of an inside track on the Scarlet Guard but I have to admit I was a little disappointed. We get to see a few familiar faces but nothing much actually happens so I found myself getting bored during this one.</span>
  <span id="freeText972261240917893766" style="display:none">Read in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25944381.Cruel_Crown__Red_Queen___0_1_0_2_" title="Cruel Crown (Red Queen, #0.1-0.2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Crown</a> bind up.<br /><br />The second story is told from the point of view of Captain Farley and starts just before <b>Red Queen</b> with some overlap in the timeline which the main reason I think you should read the full length book first. I was really excited about this story and getting more of an inside track on the Scarlet Guard but I have to admit I was a little disappointed. We get to see a few familiar faces but nothing much actually happens so I found myself getting bored during this one.<br /><br />I also wasn't a fan on the format of the coded messages sent between Farley and her point of contact, not only were they hard to understand at times but the text used for these messages was VERY repetitive which got irritating really quickly. At one point you had the phrase "<i>The following message has been decoded. Confidential, senior clearance required</i>" repeated EIGHT times in the space of three pages! It's a shame because this story could have been great but there actually seemed to be very little point to it in the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="972261240917893766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2851595801149802677">Farley was never a character I had any sort of attachment to. Not until the last chapter of GS when I realised she and Shade were in love.<br/><br/>This story was a bit boring for me up until she meets Shade for the first time.<br/><br/>I never realized that their feelings started way back then. That's what made this also so sad because of how their (Shade and Farley's) story ends.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1S2xe0M48KF3TtEHbTxKZVSQIgWWmi1KRJbNg4E3PxMINI8tFlWoVqroqlpzbRMbMvJNfqbmGVfkPkciKiW1Jg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UqY06Wi7tfNu4kVVJuF+Ui/1nDjwDaP9WRpxE3q78X2Pvwq/PdbtBLNEPgg4sCcsSZfzQ8Bxl+D5svuy0al7SA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
